 137: data class InstalledPluginRef(
 138:     val pluginId: String,
 139:     val senderId: String,
 140:     val version: String,
 141:     val installedAt: String,
 142: ) {
 143:     fun toJson(): JSONObject = JSONObject().apply {
 144:         put("plugin_id", pluginId)
 145:         put("sender_id", senderId)
 146:         put("version", version)
 147:         put("installed_at", installedAt)
 148:     }
 149: 
 150:     companion object {
 151:         fun fromJson(o: JSONObject) = InstalledPluginRef(
 152:             pluginId = o.getString("plugin_id"),
 153:             senderId = o.getString("sender_id"),
 154:             version = o.getString("version"),
 155:             installedAt = o.getString("installed_at"),
 156:         )
 157:     }
 158: }
 159: 
 160: data class DismissedMessageEntry(
 161:     val messageId: String,
 162:     val dismissedAt: String,
 163: ) {
 164:     fun toJson(): JSONObject = JSONObject().apply {
 165:         put("message_id", messageId)
 166:         put("dismissed_at", dismissedAt)
 167:     }
 168: 
 169:     companion object {
 170:         fun fromJson(o: JSONObject) = DismissedMessageEntry(
 171:             messageId = o.getString("message_id"),
 172:             dismissedAt = o.getString("dismissed_at"),
 173:         )
 174:     }
 175: }
 176: 
 177: /**
 178:  * M11.2: a message the user has marked read on at least one device. Synced
 179:  * via the M7 CAS state blob. Merge resolves conflicts by max(readAt) per
 180:  * messageId ג€” i.e. the most recently-set read timestamp wins, which works
 181:  * because "read" is a monotone state (you don't go from read to unread
 182:  * silently; a manual "mark unread" would be a separate action that writes a
 183:  * tombstone, not in V1).
 184:  */
 185: data class ReadMessageEntry(
 186:     val messageId: String,
 187:     val readAt: String,
 188: ) {
 189:     fun toJson(): JSONObject = JSONObject().apply {
 190:         put("message_id", messageId)
 191:         put("read_at", readAt)
 192:     }
 193: 
 194:     companion object {
 195:         fun fromJson(o: JSONObject) = ReadMessageEntry(
 196:             messageId = o.getString("message_id"),
 197:             readAt = o.getString("read_at"),
 198:         )
 199:     }
 200: }
 201: 
 202: /**
 203:  * M11.2: a message the user has archived. The archive state is synced via
 204:  * the M7 CAS blob so an archive on one device shows up across all of the
 205:  * user's devices.
 206:  *
 207:  * V1 semantic limit (called out in review 39 by Codex): "archived" is a
 208:  * *filter* over the still-fetchable inbox ג€” we don't persist the message
 209:  * body locally beyond the server's 30-day retention cap. Once the server
 210:  * expires the message, the archived id remains in this list but there's
 211:  * no body to render. A proper "keep past expiry" archive needs a local
 212:  * message body store and is V1.5 work. For now, treat archive as
 213:  * "hide from the active inbox while the server still has the message."
 214:  *
 215:  * Distinct from "dismiss": dismiss is a server-side message lifecycle
 216:  * action (POST /v1/messages/.../dismiss). Archive is purely the user's
 217:  * cross-device organization state.
 218:  */

 220:     val messageId: String,

   1: package app.syncler.core.storage
   2: 
   3: import android.content.Context
   4: import android.content.SharedPreferences
   5: import android.util.Base64
   6: import androidx.security.crypto.EncryptedSharedPreferences
   7: import androidx.security.crypto.MasterKey
   8: import dagger.hilt.android.qualifiers.ApplicationContext
   9: import javax.inject.Inject
  10: import javax.inject.Singleton
  11: import kotlinx.coroutines.flow.MutableStateFlow
  12: import kotlinx.coroutines.flow.StateFlow
  13: import kotlinx.coroutines.flow.asStateFlow

  15: import kotlinx.coroutines.sync.withLock
  16: import org.json.JSONObject

  18: /**
  19:  * Locally-stored paired-sender record. Locks the identity tuple at pairing
  20:  * time so future incoming messages can be verified against the same
  21:  * fingerprint + name hash + public key (I4 anti-spoofing layers 2/3/4).
  22:  */
  23: data class PairedSender(
  24:     val pairingId: String,
  25:     val senderId: String,
  26:     val senderName: String,
  27:     val senderPublicKey: ByteArray,
  28:     val fingerprint: String,
  29:     val nameHash: ByteArray,
  30:     val firstPairedAt: String,
  31:     /**
  32:      * 32-byte AES-256 key shared with the sender. Generated client-side at
  33:      * pairing time, persisted here so future messages from this sender can be
  34:      * decrypted. In V1 dev mode the user copies this off the screen and pastes
  35:      * it into the sender's CLI (`set_pairing(user_id, pairing_key_hex)`); in
  36:      * V1.5 the bootstrap exchange wires it automatically.
  37:      */
  38:     val pairingKey: ByteArray,
  39: ) {
  40:     override fun equals(other: Any?): Boolean {
  41:         if (this === other) return true
  42:         if (other !is PairedSender) return false
  43:         return pairingId == other.pairingId
  44:     }
  45: 
  46:     override fun hashCode(): Int = pairingId.hashCode()
  47: }
  48: 
  49: interface PairedSenderStore {
  50:     val pairedSenders: StateFlow<List<PairedSender>>
  51:     suspend fun add(pairedSender: PairedSender)
  52:     suspend fun remove(pairingId: String)
  53:     suspend fun byPairingId(pairingId: String): PairedSender?
  54:     suspend fun bySenderId(senderId: String): PairedSender?
  55: }
  56: 
  57: @Singleton
  58: class EncryptedPairedSenderStore @Inject constructor(
  59:     @ApplicationContext context: Context,
  60: ) : PairedSenderStore {
  61: 
  62:     private val prefs: SharedPreferences = EncryptedSharedPreferences.create(
  63:         context,
  64:         PREFS_NAME,
  65:         MasterKey.Builder(context).setKeyScheme(MasterKey.KeyScheme.AES256_GCM).build(),
  66:         EncryptedSharedPreferences.PrefKeyEncryptionScheme.AES256_SIV,
  67:         EncryptedSharedPreferences.PrefValueEncryptionScheme.AES256_GCM,
  68:     )
  69: 
  70:     private val cache = MutableStateFlow<List<PairedSender>>(loadAll())
  71:     override val pairedSenders: StateFlow<List<PairedSender>> = cache.asStateFlow()
  72:     private val mutex = Mutex()
  73: 
  74:     override suspend fun add(pairedSender: PairedSender) = mutex.withLock {
  75:         prefs.edit()
  76:             .putString(recordKey(pairedSender.pairingId), encodeRecord(pairedSender))
  77:             .apply()
  78:         updateIndex { ids -> ids + pairedSender.pairingId }
  79:         cache.value = loadAll()
  80:     }
  81: 
  82:     override suspend fun remove(pairingId: String) = mutex.withLock {
  83:         prefs.edit().remove(recordKey(pairingId)).apply()
  84:         updateIndex { ids -> ids - pairingId }
  85:         cache.value = loadAll()
  86:     }
  87: 
  88:     override suspend fun byPairingId(pairingId: String): PairedSender? =
  89:         cache.value.firstOrNull { it.pairingId == pairingId }
  90: 
  91:     override suspend fun bySenderId(senderId: String): PairedSender? =
  92:         cache.value.firstOrNull { it.senderId == senderId }
  93: 
  94:     private fun updateIndex(transform: (Set<String>) -> Set<String>) {
  95:         val current = prefs.getStringSet(KEY_IDS, emptySet()) ?: emptySet()
  96:         prefs.edit().putStringSet(KEY_IDS, transform(current)).apply()
  97:     }
  98: 
  99:     private fun recordKey(id: String) = "record:$id"
 100: 
 101:     private fun loadAll(): List<PairedSender> {
 102:         val ids = prefs.getStringSet(KEY_IDS, emptySet()) ?: emptySet()
 103:         return ids
 104:             .mapNotNull { id -> prefs.getString(recordKey(id), null)?.let(::decodeRecord) }
 105:             .sortedBy { it.firstPairedAt }
 106:     }
 107: 
 108:     private fun encodeRecord(r: PairedSender): String {
 109:         // JSON-encoded: variable-length text fields (sender name, etc.)
 110:         // cannot break parsing ג€” replaces the M6 `|` delimiter scheme.
 111:         return JSONObject().apply {
 112:             put("pairing_id", r.pairingId)
 113:             put("sender_id", r.senderId)
 114:             put("sender_name", r.senderName)
 115:             put("sender_public_key", Base64.encodeToString(r.senderPublicKey, Base64.NO_WRAP))
 116:             put("fingerprint", r.fingerprint)
 117:             put("name_hash", Base64.encodeToString(r.nameHash, Base64.NO_WRAP))
 118:             put("first_paired_at", r.firstPairedAt)
 119:             put("pairing_key", Base64.encodeToString(r.pairingKey, Base64.NO_WRAP))
 120:         }.toString()
 121:     }
 122: 
 123:     private fun decodeRecord(json: String): PairedSender? = try {
 124:         val obj = JSONObject(json)
 125:         PairedSender(
 126:             pairingId = obj.getString("pairing_id"),
 127:             senderId = obj.getString("sender_id"),
 128:             senderName = obj.getString("sender_name"),
 129:             senderPublicKey = Base64.decode(obj.getString("sender_public_key"), Base64.NO_WRAP),
 130:             fingerprint = obj.getString("fingerprint"),
 131:             nameHash = Base64.decode(obj.getString("name_hash"), Base64.NO_WRAP),
 132:             firstPairedAt = obj.getString("first_paired_at"),
 133:             pairingKey = obj.optString("pairing_key").takeIf { it.isNotBlank() }
 134:                 ?.let { Base64.decode(it, Base64.NO_WRAP) }
 135:                 ?: ByteArray(0),
 136:         )
 137:     } catch (_: Exception) {
 138:         null
 139:     }
 140: 
 141:     private companion object {
 142:         const val PREFS_NAME = "syncler.paired_senders.enc"
 143:         const val KEY_IDS = "paired_ids"
 144:     }
 145: }

  11: ---
  12: 
  13: ## Pre-flight (before any new state fields land)
  14: 
  15: **P0a ג€” Fix CAS dirty-flag bug in `UserStateRepository.push()`.**
  16: Codex Reviewer B in consultation 47 flagged that the conflict-retry
  17: failure path logs but does not throw, so `push()` can clear the dirty
  18: flag after a failed retry, losing pending pushes. Fix: ensure the
  19: dirty flag is only cleared after successful CAS upload, not after
  20: the retry-then-give-up path. Add regression test that simulates a
  21: permanent 409 conflict and verifies `dirty` remains true.
  22: 
  23: **P0b ג€” Architecture: expose state-mutation interface from `:core:storage`.**
  24: `UserStateRepository.mutateLocal` is currently private in
  25: `:feature:inbox`. Synced pairing needs it from `:core:storage`
  26: (where `PairedSenderStore` lives). Expose a small interface in
  27: `:core:storage` that `:feature:inbox` implements. No new module.
  28: 
  29: ---
  30: 
  31: ## Phase 0 ג€” Device-bound JWT + revocation enforcement
  32: 
  33: **Why first:** the lost-device threat model relies on `revoke_device`
  34: actually closing network access. Today, `/v1/state`,
  35: `/v1/messages/inbox`, and message detail only check the user JWT,
  36: not `device.revoked_at`. Synced pairing's value collapses without
  37: this.
  38: 
  39: ### Server changes
  40: 
  41: - **JWT claims now include `device_id` (`did`).** Issued at
  42:   `/v1/auth/login` after device enrollment, and refreshed at
  43:   `/v1/auth/devices/enroll` so newly-enrolled devices get a
  44:   device-bound token.
  45: - **New auth dependency `current_auth_context` in `app/auth.py`.**
  46:   Resolves user + active device. Rejects with 401 if:
  47:   - JWT missing `device_id` claim.
  48:   - Device with that ID doesn't exist.
  49:   - Device's `revoked_at IS NOT NULL`.
  50: - **Apply `current_auth_context` to all sensitive routes**:
  51:   `GET /v1/state`, `PUT /v1/state`, `GET /v1/messages/inbox`,
  52:   `GET /v1/messages/{id}`, `POST /v1/messages/{id}/dismiss`,
  53:   `GET /v1/pairing`, `POST /v1/pairing/{id}/revoke`,
  54:   `GET /v1/plugins/by-id/{id}` only when user-bound paths are
  55:   added.
  56: - **Login flow:** `/v1/auth/login` no longer returns a JWT directly;
  57:   it returns a short-lived "session bootstrap" token. The client
  58:   uses that to enroll the device, and the enroll response is the
  59:   device-bound JWT. (Or: enroll happens as part of login and the
  60:   login response includes the device-bound JWT in a single call.
  61:   Whichever has fewer moving parts; specifics in build phase.)
  62: - **Pre-existing JWTs without `device_id` are rejected.** Clients
  63:   intercept 401 with `WWW-Authenticate: device_required` and force
  64:   re-login. One-time pain.
  65: 
  66: ### Android changes
  67: 
  68: - **Session stores `deviceId`** parsed from JWT claims at login.
  69: - **`AuthRepository.login()` performs enroll-and-bind** so the
  70:   returned session token already includes `device_id`.
  71: - **401 with `device_required` triggers re-login flow** (clear
  72:   session, navigate to AuthScreen).
  73: - **Existing API call sites unaffected** ג€” they continue to pass
  74:   the JWT in `Authorization: Bearer`; the server just enforces more.
  75: 
  76: ### Tests

  80: - A device's JWT issued before its revocation is rejected after

 102: 
 103: ## Phase 1 ג€” Synced pairing via M7 encrypted state blob
 104: 
 105: ### Schema + merger
 106: 
 107: - `EncryptedUserState` gains
 108:   `pairedSenders: List<PairedSenderEntry>`. Fields:
 109:   - `pairingId` (stable per-pairing UUID)
 110:   - `senderId`, `senderName`, `senderPublicKey` (b64), `fingerprint`,
 111:     `nameHash` (b64)
 112:   - `pairingKey` (b64, 32 bytes AES-256)
 113:   - `firstPairedAt` (ISO-8601 UTC)
 114:   - `removedAt` (nullable; tombstone)
 115:   - `source` (string; `"manual"` for new pairings, `"migration"` for
 116:     bootstrapped entries from first launch)
 117: - Bump `SCHEMA_CURRENT` to V4. Forward-migration handles V0..V3
 118:   emitting empty `pairedSenders`.
 119: - `StateMerger` per-`pairingId` merge:
 120:   - **Tombstone wins** ג€” if either side has `removedAt` set, the
 121:     later `removedAt` survives (or, if only one side has it, that
 122:     side wins).
 123:   - **Add conflict:** oldest `firstPairedAt` wins (deterministic;
 124:     near-impossible in practice since pairingIds are fresh UUIDs).
 125: 
 126: ### Local store integration
 127: 
 128: - **`PairedSenderStore` becomes a projection of
 129:   `UserStateRepository.state`.** Observer pattern (mirrors
 130:   read-mark / archive / delete model).
 131: - **Adds:** `PairingRepository.confirm(...)` writes BOTH to local
 132:   encrypted prefs AND calls `userStateRepository.mutateLocal { it.add(...) }`.
 133:   Same `markDirtyAndPush` pattern as read marks.
 134: - **Removes:** `PairingRepository.revoke(...)` writes tombstone to
 135:   synced state AND wipes local key bytes (zero out the byte array
 136:   before removing from prefs).
 137: 
 138: ### First-run migration (one-time bootstrap)
 139: 
 140: - On first unlocked launch after `SCHEMA_CURRENT` bumps to V4:
 141:   1. Read all `PairedSender` entries from local
 142:      `EncryptedSharedPreferences`.
 143:   2. For each entry not already in synced state, push via
 144:      `mutateLocal`, marked `source: "migration"`.
 145:   3. Guard with a `pairing_sync_migration_done` flag in local prefs
 146:      so this only happens once per device.
 147: - **Non-blocking review banner:** post-migration, inbox shows a
 148:   one-time banner: *"Your paired senders are now synced across your
 149:   devices. Review them in the Senders tab."* Dismissable.
 150: - The banner is local-only (not synced). Each device shows it once
 151:   on its own migration. No mandatory review gate.
 152: 
 153: ### Decryption tolerates multiple active keys per sender
 154: 
 155: - `InboxRepository.refresh()` already iterates pairings by
 156:   `senderId`. Extend: if multiple non-tombstoned pairings exist for
 157:   the same `senderId` (legacy transition state), try each pairing
 158:   key in turn until one decrypts cleanly. Tombstoned entries
 159:   skipped entirely.
 160: 
 161: ### Re-pair semantics
 162: 
 163: - On a new pairing for an existing `senderId`, tombstone the old
 164:   pairing in the same `mutateLocal` write atomically. After commit,
 165:   `bySenderId()` returns the newest active pairing.
 166: 
 167: ### Lost-device guidance in integration guide
 168: 
 169: - Add a "Lost device" section with the three-step user procedure:
 170:   1. Revoke the device from Settings ג†’ Devices.
 171:   2. For each sender that handled sensitive data, re-pair on a
 172:      trusted device (this rotates that sender's key).
 173:   3. Past cached data on the lost device is unrecoverable.
 174: - Note that the guided rotation flow is future roadmap.
 175: 
 176: ### Tests
 177: 
 178: - Schema migration V0..V3 ג†’ V4 preserves existing fields, emits
 179:   empty `pairedSenders`.
 180: - Two devices migrating local pairings concurrently ג†’ CAS merge
 181:   result is the union (with deduplication by `pairingId`).
 182: - Re-pair tombstones old, new pairing is active, `bySenderId`
 183:   returns newest.
 184: - Multi-key decryption: messages encrypted with either of two
 185:   active pairing keys decrypt; with a tombstoned key, fails.
 186: - Tombstone resurrection prevented: offline device with stale local
 187:   state including an active pairing that's been tombstoned post-sync
 188:   does not resurrect the pairing on its next state push.
 189: - Migration: bootstrapped pairings land in synced state with
 190:   `source: "migration"`; subsequent launches don't re-push.
 191: - Migration banner: shown once, dismissable, not synced.
 192: - Lifecycle: revoked device's `PUT /v1/state` rejected (Phase 0
 193:   hardening).
 194: 
 195: ### Out of scope
 196: 
 197: - SSE delivery of state changes (Phase 2).
 198: - Templates / live cards / settings sheet (Phase 3).
 199: - Guided lost-device rotation flow (future roadmap).

  51: @Singleton
  52: class UserStateRepository @Inject constructor(
  53:     private val prefs: UserStatePrefs,
  54:     private val api: SynclerApi,
  55:     private val session: Session,
  56:     private val clock: Clock = Clock.systemUTC(),
  57: ) : UserStateMutator {
  58:     private val scope = CoroutineScope(SupervisorJob() + Dispatchers.IO)
  59: 
  60:     init {
  61:         // Auto-clear local state when the session locks (logout, JWT expiry,
  62:         // process restart without password). Without this, a subsequent
  63:         // login on the same device would inherit the previous user's read
  64:         // marks AND push them up to the new user's server account.

 230:         runCatching {
 231:             val response = api.getUserState()
 232:             val remoteState = decodeRemote(response.encryptedBlob, masterKey)
 233:             val merged = StateMerger.merge(local = _state.value, remote = remoteState)
 234:             _state.value = merged
 235:             persist(merged, remoteVersion = response.stateVersion)
 236:         }.onFailure { Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "pull failed") }
 237:     }
 238: 
 239:     /**
 240:      * Encrypts the local state and PUTs to the server with the last-known
 241:      * CAS version. On 409 conflict: pull-merge-retry once. No-op when the
 242:      * session is locked. Successful push clears the dirty flag.
 243:      */
 244:     suspend fun push(): Result<Unit> = syncMutex.withLock {
 245:         val masterKey = session.sessionState.value.masterKey ?: return@withLock Result.success(Unit)
 246:         // Defensive: a future-schema blob (downloaded by a newer client and
 247:         // somehow persisted on this older one) should NOT be pushed back ג€”
 248:         // we'd write known fields under the future schema_version, losing
 249:         // the V3+ fields the newer client wrote. Refuse-to-push surfaces the
 250:         // version skew as a push failure rather than corrupting state.
 251:         if (_state.value.schemaVersion > EncryptedUserState.SCHEMA_CURRENT) {
 252:             Timber.tag(TAG).w(
 253:                 "refusing to push schema_version %d (client supports %d)",
 254:                 _state.value.schemaVersion, EncryptedUserState.SCHEMA_CURRENT,
 255:             )
 256:             return@withLock Result.failure(IllegalStateException("future schema; refusing to push"))
 257:         }
 258:         runCatching {
 259:             attemptPush(masterKey)
 260:             clearDirty()
 261:         }.onFailure { Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "push failed (after retry)") }
 262:     }
 263: 
 264:     private suspend fun attemptPush(masterKey: ByteArray) {
 265:         val blob = encodeLocal(_state.value, masterKey)
 266:         val expected = lastKnownRemoteVersion()
 267:         try {
 268:             val response = api.putUserState(
 269:                 StatePutRequestDto(
 270:                     expectedStateVersion = expected,
 271:                     newEncryptedBlob = blob,
 272:                 ),
 273:             )
 274:             if (!response.isSuccessful) {
 275:                 if (response.code() == 409) {
 276:                     handleConflictAndRetry(masterKey)
 277:                 } else {
 278:                     throw HttpException(response)
 279:                 }
 280:             } else {
 281:                 response.body()?.newStateVersion?.let { setLastKnownRemoteVersion(it) }
 282:             }
 283:         } catch (e: HttpException) {
 284:             if (e.code() == 409) handleConflictAndRetry(masterKey) else throw e
 285:         }
 286:     }
 287: 
 288:     private suspend fun handleConflictAndRetry(masterKey: ByteArray) {
 289:         // Server has a newer blob. Pull, merge, re-push exactly once. If the
 290:         // retry also fails, THROW so push()'s runCatching catches it and
 291:         // skips clearDirty() ג€” the dirty flag must stay true so the next
 292:         // foreground tick (flushPendingPush) retries again.
 293:         //
 294:         // Codex review 47 (consultation 47, Reviewer B): the previous
 295:         // implementation silently logged the retry-failure path, which let
 296:         // push()'s outer runCatching reach clearDirty() and lose the
 297:         // pending change. That bug is fixed here.
 298:         val response = api.getUserState()
 299:         val remoteState = decodeRemote(response.encryptedBlob, masterKey)
 300:         val merged = StateMerger.merge(local = _state.value, remote = remoteState)
 301:         _state.value = merged
 302:         persist(merged, remoteVersion = response.stateVersion)
 303: 
 304:         val newBlob = encodeLocal(_state.value, masterKey)
 305:         val retry = api.putUserState(
 306:             StatePutRequestDto(
 307:                 expectedStateVersion = response.stateVersion,
 308:                 newEncryptedBlob = newBlob,
 309:             ),
 310:         )

  45:  * dirty flag remains true after push() returns failure.
  46:  */

codex
The CAS throw is catchable by `push()`’s `runCatching`, but the current `attemptPush` catch also intercepts the retry’s 409 and runs conflict handling a second time. That is not the original dirty-flag loss, but it is a retry-count/control-flow issue worth fixing while this is still foundation work.

   5: /**
   6:  * Cross-module write surface for the encrypted user state blob.
   7:  *
   8:  * Implemented by `:feature:inbox.UserStateRepository` (which owns the blob,
   9:  * the master-key access, the CAS sync, and the disk persistence). Exposed
  10:  * via an interface in `:core:storage` so other `:core:storage` components
  11:  * ג€” notably `PairedSenderStore` in the synced-pairing phase ג€” can mutate
  12:  * the synced state without depending on the inbox feature module.
  13:  *
  14:  * Implementations must:
  15:  *  - apply [mutateAndPush]'s transform atomically against the current state
  16:  *  - persist the new state locally before scheduling the push
  17:  *  - schedule a CAS-backed push so other devices receive the change
  18:  *  - silently accept calls while the session is locked (the dirty flag
  19:  *    survives, and the push happens on next unlock)
  20:  *
  21:  * The `state` flow emits the latest local state on every change.
  22:  */
  23: interface UserStateMutator {
  24:     val state: StateFlow<EncryptedUserState>
  25: 
  26:     /**
  27:      * Atomically applies [transform] to the current state, persists the
  28:      * result locally, marks the state dirty, and schedules a push to the
  29:      * server. Safe to call concurrently ג€” the implementation serializes
  30:      * mutations.
  31:      */
  32:     suspend fun mutateAndPush(transform: (EncryptedUserState) -> EncryptedUserState)
  33: }

 130:     request.state.user_id = str(user.id)

 133: 
 134: async def current_auth_context(
 135:     request: Request,
 136:     token: str = Depends(oauth2_scheme),
 137:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 138: ) -> AuthContext:
 139:     """Resolves user + device for sensitive routes.
 140: 
 141:     Rejects requests where:
 142:     - The token lacks a `did` claim (pre-Phase-0 tokens; the
 143:       `WWW-Authenticate: device_required` hint tells clients to re-login
 144:       so the enrollment flow runs and a device-bound token is issued).
 145:     - The device does not exist (e.g. enrollment was rolled back).
 146:     - The device has been revoked (`revoked_at` is set).
 147: 
 148:     Returns an [AuthContext] so handlers can read `ctx.user` and
 149:     `ctx.device` directly.
 150:     """
 151:     claims = _decode_claims(token)
 152:     if claims.device_id is None:
 153:         raise HTTPException(
 154:             status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED,
 155:             detail="device-bound token required; re-login to enroll",
 156:             headers={"WWW-Authenticate": "device_required"},
 157:         )
 158:     user = await get_user_by_id(db, claims.user_id)
 159:     if user is None:
 160:         raise HTTPException(
 161:             status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED,
 162:             detail="invalid token",
 163:             headers={"WWW-Authenticate": "Bearer"},
 164:         )
 165:     device_row = await db.execute(
 166:         select(Device).where(Device.id == claims.device_id, Device.user_id == user.id),
 167:     )
 168:     device = device_row.scalar_one_or_none()
 169:     if device is None:
 170:         raise HTTPException(
 171:             status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED,
 172:             detail="device not enrolled",
 173:             headers={"WWW-Authenticate": "device_required"},
 174:         )
 175:     if device.revoked_at is not None:
 176:         raise HTTPException(
 177:             status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED,
 178:             detail="device revoked",
 179:             headers={"WWW-Authenticate": "device_revoked"},
 180:         )
 181:     request.state.user_id = str(user.id)
 182:     request.state.device_id = str(device.id)
 183:     return AuthContext(user=user, device=device)

  61: async def auth_header(client: AsyncClient, email: str = "device-user@example.com", fill: int = 1) -> dict[str, str]:
  62:     """Return an auth header for a device-bound JWT.
  63: 
  64:     Phase 0 (device-bound JWT): sensitive routes (list_devices, revoke,
  65:     state, inbox, message detail, dismiss) require a token with a `did`
  66:     claim. The bootstrap login token does NOT carry that claim; the
  67:     enroll response does. This helper does both so callers get a token
  68:     that works on every authenticated route the device tests touch.
  69:     """
  70:     payload = signup_payload(email=email, auth_key_hash=b64_bytes(32, fill))
  71:     await client.post("/v1/auth/signup", json=payload)
  72:     login = await client.post(
  73:         "/v1/auth/login",
  74:         json={"email": payload["email"], "auth_key_hash": payload["auth_key_hash"]},
  75:     )
  76:     bootstrap_headers = {"Authorization": f"Bearer {login.json()['session_token']}"}
  77:     enroll = await client.post(
  78:         "/v1/auth/devices/enroll",
  79:         json={"public_key": b64_bytes(32, fill + 10)},
  80:         headers=bootstrap_headers,
  81:     )
  82:     return {"Authorization": f"Bearer {enroll.json()['session_token']}"}
  83: 
  84: 
  85: async def bootstrap_only_header(client: AsyncClient, email: str = "bootstrap-only@example.com", fill: int = 99) -> dict[str, str]:
  86:     """Return a header for the user-only bootstrap token from login (no
  87:     device enrolled). Used by tests that need to verify sensitive routes
  88:     reject pre-device tokens."""
  89:     payload = signup_payload(email=email, auth_key_hash=b64_bytes(32, fill))
  90:     await client.post("/v1/auth/signup", json=payload)
  91:     login = await client.post(
  92:         "/v1/auth/login",
  93:         json={"email": payload["email"], "auth_key_hash": payload["auth_key_hash"]},
  94:     )
  95:     return {"Authorization": f"Bearer {login.json()['session_token']}"}

  51: def _sign_initiate(private_key: Ed25519PrivateKey, *, sender_id: uuid.UUID, ttl: int, metadata: dict) -> str:

  53:     canonical = json.dumps(body, sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":")).encode("utf-8")
  54:     return _b64(private_key.sign(canonical))

   1: package app.syncler.core.network
   2: 
   3: import com.squareup.moshi.Moshi
   4: import dagger.Module
   5: import dagger.Provides
   6: import dagger.multibindings.Multibinds
   7: import dagger.hilt.InstallIn
   8: import dagger.hilt.components.SingletonComponent
   9: import javax.inject.Singleton
  10: import okhttp3.ConnectionSpec
  11: import okhttp3.Interceptor
  12: import okhttp3.OkHttpClient
  13: import okhttp3.logging.HttpLoggingInterceptor
  14: import retrofit2.Retrofit
  15: import retrofit2.converter.moshi.MoshiConverterFactory
  16: 
  17: @Module
  18: @InstallIn(SingletonComponent::class)
  19: abstract class AuthTokenProviderSetModule {
  20:     @Multibinds
  21:     abstract fun authTokenProviders(): Set<AuthTokenProvider>
  22: }
  23: 
  24: @Module
  25: @InstallIn(SingletonComponent::class)
  26: object NetworkModule {
  27:     @Provides
  28:     @Singleton
  29:     fun provideMoshi(): Moshi = Moshi.Builder().build()
  30: 
  31:     @Provides
  32:     @Singleton
  33:     fun provideAuthInterceptor(tokenProviders: Set<@JvmSuppressWildcards AuthTokenProvider>): Interceptor =
  34:         Interceptor { chain ->
  35:             val token = tokenProviders.firstNotNullOfOrNull { it.currentToken() }
  36:             val request = if (token.isNullOrBlank()) {
  37:                 chain.request()
  38:             } else {
  39:                 chain.request().newBuilder()
  40:                     .header("Authorization", "Bearer $token")
  41:                     .build()
  42:             }
  43:             chain.proceed(request)
  44:         }
  45: 
  46:     @Provides
  47:     @Singleton
  48:     fun provideOkHttpClient(authInterceptor: Interceptor): OkHttpClient {
  49:         val logging = HttpLoggingInterceptor().apply {
  50:             level = HttpLoggingInterceptor.Level.BASIC
  51:         }
  52:         // OkHttp's default connectionSpecs is [MODERN_TLS, COMPATIBLE_TLS]
  53:         // and refuses cleartext at the connection layer. Debug builds point
  54:         // SERVER_BASE_URL at http://10.0.2.2:8000/ (or a LAN IP), so we need
  55:         // CLEARTEXT in the spec list for dev. Release stays HTTPS-only.
  56:         return OkHttpClient.Builder()
  57:             .addInterceptor(authInterceptor)
  58:             .addInterceptor(logging)
  59:             .connectionSpecs(
  60:                 if (BuildConfig.DEBUG) {

 328:      * Wipes all persisted state and resets to empty. Invoked automatically

codex
**Reviewer: Codex**

**Findings**

1. **RED: revoked/device-bound tokens can still mint a fresh active device.**  
   [server/app/routers/devices.py:18](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/routers/devices.py:18) uses `current_user` for `/v1/auth/devices/enroll`, and [server/app/auth.py:110](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/auth.py:110) ignores `did` and `revoked_at`. A revoked device-bound JWT can call enroll, get a new `session_token`, and regain access. This defeats the Phase 0 revocation guarantee. Fix with a bootstrap-only auth dependency that rejects `did` tokens, or validate `did` tokens for revocation before allowing enroll. Also make bootstrap tokens short-lived and scoped; currently they use the same 24h expiry at [server/app/auth.py:73](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/auth.py:73).

2. **RED: sensitive user routes still use user-only auth.**  
   Pairing still uses `current_user` for complete/list/revoke at [server/app/routers/pairing.py:155](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/routers/pairing.py:155), [server/app/routers/pairing.py:206](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/routers/pairing.py:206), and [server/app/routers/pairing.py:218](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/routers/pairing.py:218). Account deletion also uses `current_user` at [server/app/routers/auth.py:96](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/routers/auth.py:96). A revoked device can still mutate pairings or delete the account. Senders/plugins are okay as public/sender-signed surfaces; `/plugins/by-id` matches the plan’s “only when user-bound paths are added” caveat.

3. **RED: Android Hilt likely fails to compile.**  
   [UserStateRepository.kt:56](/D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/UserStateRepository.kt:56) moved `Clock` into the `@Inject` constructor with a default value. Dagger/Hilt still treats that as an injectable dependency, and there is no `Clock` binding. Restore a private `Clock.systemUTC()` production field plus a test-only secondary constructor, or add an explicit `@Provides Clock`.

4. **YELLOW: login publishes the bootstrap token as an unlocked session before enrollment finishes.**  
   [AuthRepository.kt:79](/D:/Projects/syncler/android/core/auth/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/core/auth/AuthRepository.kt:79) calls `session.authenticate(response.sessionToken, masterKey)` before [AuthRepository.kt:80](/D:/Projects/syncler/android/core/auth/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/core/auth/AuthRepository.kt:80) enrolls and swaps at [Session.kt:66](/D:/Projects/syncler/android/core/auth/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/core/auth/Session.kt:66). Any observer that reacts to `isUnlocked=true` can start sensitive requests with the bootstrap token and get `device_required`. Avoid exposing unlocked state until the device-bound token is installed.

5. **YELLOW: CAS retry throw is catchable, but the control flow retries twice.**  
   The retry failure throws at [UserStateRepository.kt:318](/D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/UserStateRepository.kt:318). That is catchable by `push()`’s outer `runCatching`, but first it is caught by `attemptPush()` at [UserStateRepository.kt:283](/D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/UserStateRepository.kt:283), which calls `handleConflictAndRetry()` again at [UserStateRepository.kt:284](/D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/UserStateRepository.kt:284). The dirty flag survives, but “retry once” is now effectively “retry twice.” Narrow the catch or return after the explicit 409 handling.

6. **YELLOW: unchanged tests are inconsistent with the new auth contract.**  
   `server/tests/test_state.py` still sends the bootstrap token to `/v1/state` at [test_state.py:38](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/tests/test_state.py:38). `test_auth.py` and the integration auth/device test similarly use the pre-enroll token after enrollment at [test_auth.py:214](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/tests/test_auth.py:214) and [test_integration_auth_devices.py:45](/D:/Projects/syncler/server/tests/test_integration_auth_devices.py:45). These should use the enroll response’s `session_token`.

**Per-Task Verdicts**

- **0a CAS dirty-flag fix:** yellow. Core dirty-flag loss is fixed, but retry control flow should be corrected and the regression test should assert failure and expected PUT count. Minor warning: unused `SessionStore` import at [UserStateRepositoryPushTest.kt:4](/D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/test/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/UserStateRepositoryPushTest.kt:4).
- **0b `UserStateMutator`:** red until the Hilt `Clock` constructor issue is fixed. The interface shape is acceptable for Phase 1; `mutateAndPush` is enough for batched transforms, and `:core:storage` already has Hilt dependencies.
- **0 main device-bound JWT:** red. Revocation is bypassable through enroll/account/pairing routes, and bootstrap scope/lifetime is too broad.

**Cross-Cutting**

No missed Android `api.inbox(...)` or `dismissMessage(...)` call sites found. FastAPI will ignore stale `?device_id=...` query params on `/v1/messages/inbox`, but old clients without `did` correctly get 401 once route auth is fixed. `assert_device_belongs_to_user` is now only left in the service layer; harmless but dead unless future code reuses it.

**Recommendation**

Hold for fix-ups before Phase 1. The minimum landing set is: bootstrap-only enroll auth, move pairing/account to `current_auth_context`, fix the Hilt `Clock` injection, update stale server tests, and clean up the CAS retry control flow. I could not run verification here: pytest is missing `sqlalchemy`, and Gradle failed on an inaccessible wrapper lock file.
